**Target Repositories (version-pinned mirrors):**

Scope ALL keyword_search/nls_search queries to these repos.
Use the repo name as the `repo` parameter for read_file/go_to_definition/find_references.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |

| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Investigation: Dashboard Migration v38 Table Panel Regression

**Repository:** github.com/sg-evals/grafana--26d36ec (mirror of grafana/grafana)
**Task Type:** Regression Hunt (investigation only — no code fixes)

## Scenario

After upgrading Grafana from v10.3 to v10.4, some dashboards with table panels fail to render correctly. The table panel's field override configuration is silently dropped during dashboard import. Users see tables with missing column formatting (column widths, text alignment, cell display modes).

The bug only affects dashboards where `fieldConfig.defaults.custom` was not explicitly set in the saved dashboard JSON. Dashboards with explicit custom config render correctly.

## Your Task

Investigate the root cause and produce a report at `/logs/agent/investigation.md`.

Your report MUST cover:
1. Which migration function is responsible for the regression
2. The exact conditional logic that fails for dashboards without explicit `defaults.custom`
3. Why dashboards with explicit `defaults.custom` are unaffected
4. Which dashboard schema version triggers the issue
5. The files and functions involved in the migration chain

## Output Requirements

Write your investigation report to `/logs/agent/investigation.md` with these sections:

```
# Investigation Report

## Summary
<1-2 sentence finding>

## Root Cause
<Specific file, function, and mechanism>

## Evidence
<Code references with file paths and line numbers>

## Affected Components
<List of packages/modules impacted>

## Recommendation
<Fix strategy>
```

## Constraints

- Do NOT write any code fixes
- Do NOT modify any source files
- Your job is investigation and analysis only
- Focus on the dashboard migration pipeline, particularly schema version handlers

36-assistanttext-
Based on my investigation, I've identified the root cause of the dashboard migration regression. Let me create the investigation report:
37-assistanttool_useWrite
38-usertool_resultWrite
File created successfully at: /logs/agent/investigation.md
39-assistanttext-
Perfect! I've completed the investigation and created a comprehensive report at `/logs/agent/investigation.md`. Here's a summary of what I found:

## Key Findings

**Root Cause:** The V38 migration has an asymmetry in how it handles table panels without explicit `fieldConfig.defaults.custom`:

1. **The Migration** (v38.go:115-127): Only processes `defaults.custom` if it already exists - it does NOT create it
2. **The Tracking** (frontend_defaults.go:1138-1169): Only sets `_originallyHadFieldConfigCustom = true` if custom exists in the original
3. **The Cleanup** (frontend_defaults.go:606-620): Only preserves the custom structure during cleanup if the tracking flag is set

**The Failure Scenario:**
- A table panel without explicit `defaults.custom` has field overrides with `custom.displayMode`
- V38 migration converts those overrides to `custom.cellOptions` correctly
- BUT `defaults.custom` is NOT created (intentional design)
- The tracking flag is NOT set (because original didn't have custom)
- During cleanup, the preservation logic is skipped
- This leaves a structural inconsistency: overrides reference `custom.*` but defaults lacks the `custom` container

**Why dashboards WITH explicit `defaults.custom` work:** The tracking flag IS set when custom exists, triggering the cleanup preservation logic that recreates the structure.

The report includes exact file references (v38.go, frontend_defaults.go, migrate.go) with line numbers, a test case that documents the exact scenario, and specific recommendations for fixing the asymmetry to ensure structural consistency between field defaults and overrides.

        

      

      

        Tool Calls (15)

  "content": "# Investigation Report: Dashboard Migration v38 Table Panel Regression\n\n## Summary\n\nThe v38 migration fails to preserve table panel field override configurations when dashboards don't have explicit `fieldConfig.defaults.custom` in the original JSON. During the cleanup phase, field overrides with `custom.displayMode` are correctly migrated to `custom.cellOptions` by the V38 backend migration, but the absence of `defaults.custom` causes the field override structure to be inconsistently preserved, resulting in a mismatch between override references and default configuration structure.\n\n## Root Cause\n\nThe regression occurs due to an asymmetry in how the v38 migration and cleanup phase handle panels without explicit `fieldConfig.defaults.custom`:\n\n### Migration Phase (v38.go:115-127)\n```go\n// Process defaults.custom if it exists\nif defaults, ok := fieldConfig[\"defaults\"].(map[string]interface{}); ok {\n    if custom, ok := defaults[\"custom\"].(map[string]interface{}); ok {\n        // Only process if custom exists - custom is NOT created here\n    }\n}\n// Field overrides ARE migrated regardless (line 131)\nmigrateOverrides(fieldConfig)\n```\n\nThe V38 migration intentionally does NOT create `fieldConfig.defaults.custom` when it doesn't exist. Instead, it only migrates field overrides that reference `custom.displayMode` to `custom.cellOptions` (lines 129-131).\n\n### Tracking Phase (frontend_defaults.go:1138-1169)\n```go\n// Track original presence of fieldConfig.defaults.custom\nfunc trackOriginalFieldConfigCustom(dashboard map[string]interface{}) {\n    // Only sets _originallyHadFieldConfigCustom = true if custom EXISTS\n    // Does NOT set it if custom is missing\n}\n```\n\nThe tracking function marks panels with `_originallyHadFieldConfigCustom = true` ONLY if `defaults.custom` already exists in the input. For panels without explicit `custom`, this flag is never set.\n\n### Cleanup Phase (frontend_defaults.go:606-620)\n```go\nif prop == \"fieldConfig\" {\n    // Only preserves custom if panel[\"_originallyHadFieldConfigCustom\"] == true\n    if panel[\"_originallyHadFieldConfigCustom\"] == true {\n        // Recreate defaults.custom structure\n    }\n    delete(panel, prop)  // Deletes entire fieldConfig if not marked as original\n}\n```\n\nDuring the cleanup phase, the logic depends on the `_originallyHadFieldConfigCustom` flag to decide whether to preserve the `fieldConfig.defaults.custom` structure. For panels that didn't originally have `custom`, this flag is false, so the preservation logic is skipped.\n\n## The Failure Scenario\n\nFor a table panel with `fieldConfig: { defaults: {}, overrides: [{id: \"custom.displayMode\", value: \"color-background\"}] }`:\n\n1. **trackOriginalFieldConfigCustom** runs: Since `defaults.custom` doesn't exist, it does NOT set `_originallyHadFieldConfigCustom = true`\n2. **V38 migration** runs:\n   - Skips defaults processing (line 116-127) because `defaults.custom` doesn't exist\n   - Successfully migrates override from `custom.displayMode` to `custom.cellOptions` (line 131)\n   - **Does NOT create `defaults.custom`** (intentional design)\n3. **Cleanup phase** runs:\n   - Checks if `_originallyHadFieldConfigCustom == true`: **FALSE** (because original didn't have it)\n   - Preservation logic is skipped\n   - Field overrides now reference `custom.cellOptions`, but `defaults.custom` is still missing\n   - The fieldConfig structure becomes inconsistent: overrides reference `custom.*` properties, but defaults doesn't define `custom`\n\n## Exact Conditional Logic Failure\n\n**File:** `apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/schemaversion/v38.go`, lines 115-127\n\n**Problem:** The condition `if custom, ok := defaults[\"custom\"].(map[string]interface{})` only processes `defaults.custom` if it already exists. It does NOT create it.\n\n```go\n// Lines 115-127: Only processes if custom exists\nif defaults, ok := fieldConfig[\"defaults\"].(map[string]interface{}); ok {\n    if custom, ok := defaults[\"custom\"].(map[string]interface{}); ok {\n        // Migrate displayMode to cellOptions ONLY if custom exists\n        if displayMode, exists := custom[\"displayMode\"]; exists {\n            if displayModeStr, ok := displayMode.(string); ok {\n                custom[\"cellOptions\"] = migrateTableDisplayModeToCellOptions(displayModeStr)\n            }\n            delete(custom, \"displayMode\")\n        }\n    }\n}\n// Line 129-131: ALWAYS migrate overrides, but doesn't ensure defaults.custom exists\nmigrateOverrides(fieldConfig)\n```\n\n**Why dashboards with explicit `defaults.custom` work:** If the original dashboard had `defaults.custom`, the `trackOriginalFieldConfigCustom` function sets the flag to true, causing the cleanup phase to preserve/recreate the `custom` structure, maintaining structural consistency.\n\n## Evidence\n\n### Backend Code References\n- **File:** `apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/schemaversion/v38.go`\n  - Lines 75-87: V38 function entry point\n  - Lines 115-127: Defaults.custom processing (conditional)\n  - Lines 129-131: Override migration (unconditional)\n  - Lines 136-176: migrateOverrides function\n\n- **File:** `apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/frontend_defaults.go`\n  - Lines 1138-1148: trackOriginalFieldConfigCustom (ONLY marks if custom exists)\n  - Lines 606-620: Cleanup fieldConfig preservation (depends on _originallyHadFieldConfigCustom flag)\n\n### Test Case Evidence\n- **File:** `apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/schemaversion/v38_test.go`\n  - Lines 444-554: Test case \"table with missing defaults.custom but overrides with custom.displayMode\"\n  - This test documents the exact scenario where defaults.custom is missing but overrides have custom.displayMode\n  - The test expects successful migration, indicating the backend code SHOULD handle this case\n\n### Frontend Migration (for reference)\n- **File:** `public/app/features/dashboard/state/DashboardMigrator.ts`\n  - Lines 644-674: Frontend V38 migration\n  - Lines 659-669: Override migration in frontend (also executed)\n  - Frontend expects both defaults and overrides to be properly structured\n\n## Affected Components\n\n1. **Backend Dashboard Migration**: `apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/schemaversion/v38.go`\n   - Table panel displayMode to cellOptions conversion\n   - Only partially creates required data structures\n\n2. **Frontend Defaults Application**: `apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/frontend_defaults.go`\n   - `trackOriginalFieldConfigCustom()` function (lines 1138-1169)\n   - `filterDefaultValues()` cleanup phase (lines 557-662)\n   - Field structure preservation logic\n\n3. **Dashboard Migration Pipeline**: `apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/migrate.go`\n   - Migration execution order (tracking before defaults, defaults before migration, cleanup after migration)\n\n4. **Test Coverage**: `apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/schemaversion/v38_test.go`\n   - Test case correctly identifies the scenario but may not verify field override functionality\n\n## Recommendation\n\n**Fix Strategy:** Ensure that when V38 migration processes field overrides that reference `custom.*` properties, it must also ensure that `fieldConfig.defaults.custom` exists, even if it was not originally present in the input.\n\n**Specific Action:** In `v38.go`, modify the migrateOverrides call to be preceded by ensuring defaults.custom structure exists:\n\n```go\n// Before migrating overrides, ensure defaults.custom exists\n// if there are custom override properties\nmigrateOverridesWithDefaults(fieldConfig, panel)\n```\n\nThis ensures structural consistency: if field overrides reference `custom.cellOptions`, the defaults must have a corresponding `custom` object, even if empty.\n\n**Alternatively:** Modify the cleanup phase in `frontend_defaults.go` to preserve `fieldConfig.defaults.custom` for table panels if their overrides contain any `custom.*` property references, regardless of the `_originallyHadFieldConfigCustom` flag.\n\nThe core principle: **Field override and field default structures must be symmetrical** - if overrides reference `custom.*`, the defaults must provide the `custom` container object.\n",

Instead, it only migrates field overrides that reference `custom.displayMode` to `custom.cellOptions` (lines 129-131).\n\n### Tracking Phase (frontend_defaults.go:1138-1169)\n```go\n// Track original presence of fieldConfig.defaults.custom\nfunc trackOriginalFieldConfigCustom(dashboard map[string]interface{}) {\n    // Only sets _originallyHadFieldConfigCustom = true if custom EXISTS\n    // Does NOT set it if custom is missing\n}\n```\n\nThe tracking function marks panels with `_originallyHadFieldConfigCustom = true` ONLY if `defaults.custom` already exists in the input. It does NOT create it.\n\n```go\n// Lines 115-127: Only processes if custom exists\nif defaults, ok := fieldConfig[\"defaults\"].(map[string]interface{}); ok {\n    if custom, ok := defaults[\"custom\"].(map[string]interface{}); ok {\n        // Migrate displayMode to cellOptions ONLY if custom exists\n        if displayMode, exists := custom[\"displayMode\"]; exists {\n            if displayModeStr, ok := displayMode.(string); ok {\n                custom[\"cellOptions\"] = migrateTableDisplayModeToCellOptions(displayModeStr)\n            }\n            delete(custom, \"displayMode\")\n        }\n    }\n}\n// Line 129-131: ALWAYS migrate overrides, but doesn't ensure defaults.custom exists\nmigrateOverrides(fieldConfig)\n```\n\n**Why dashboards with explicit `defaults.custom` work:** If the original dashboard had `defaults.custom`, the `trackOriginalFieldConfigCustom` function sets the flag to true, causing the cleanup phase to preserve/recreate the `custom` structure, maintaining structural consistency.\n\n## Evidence\n\n### Backend Code References\n- **File:** `apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/schemaversion/v38.go`\n  - # Investigation Report: Dashboard Migration v38 Table Panel Regression

## Summary

The v38 migration fails to preserve table panel field override configurations when dashboards don't have explicit `fieldConfig.defaults.custom` in the original JSON. During the cleanup phase, field overrides with `custom.displayMode` are correctly migrated to `custom.cellOptions` by the V38 backend migration, but the absence of `defaults.custom` causes the field override structure to be inconsistently preserved, resulting in a mismatch between override references and default configuration structure.

## Root Cause

The regression occurs due to an asymmetry in how the v38 migration and cleanup phase handle panels without explicit `fieldConfig.defaults.custom`:

### Migration Phase (v38.go:115-127)
```go
// Process defaults.custom if it exists
if defaults, ok := fieldConfig["defaults"].(map[string]interface{}); ok {
    if custom, ok := defaults["custom"].(map[string]interface{}); ok {
        // Only process if custom exists - custom is NOT created here
    }
}
// Field overrides ARE migrated regardless (line 131)
migrateOverrides(fieldConfig)
```

The V38 migration intentionally does NOT create `fieldConfig.defaults.custom` when it doesn't exist. Instead, it only migrates field overrides that reference `custom.displayMode` to `custom.cellOptions` (lines 129-131).

### Tracking Phase (frontend_defaults.go:1138-1169)
```go
// Track original presence of fieldConfig.defaults.custom
func trackOriginalFieldConfigCustom(dashboard map[string]interface{}) {
    // Only sets _originallyHadFieldConfigCustom = true if custom EXISTS
    // Does NOT set it if custom is missing
}
```

The tracking function marks panels with `_originallyHadFieldConfigCustom = true` ONLY if `defaults.custom` already exis
... (truncated)
